        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.3c03386"><meta property="og:title" content="Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03386/asset/images/acsami.3c03386.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Though layered sodium oxide materials are identified as promising cathodes in sodium-ion batteries, biphasic P3/O3 depicts improved electrochemical performance and structural stability. Herein, a coexistent P3/O3 biphasic cathode material was synthesized with “LiF” integration, verified with X-ray diffraction and Rietveld refinement analysis. Furthermore, the presence of Li and F was deduced by inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectrometry (ICP-OES) and energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS). The biphasic P3/O3 cathode displayed an excellent capacity retention of 85% after 100 cycles (0.2C/30 mA g–1) at room temperature and 94% at −20 °C after 100 cycles (0.1C/15 mA g–1) with superior rate capability as compared to the pristine cathode. Furthermore, a full cell comprising a hard carbon anode and a biphasic cathode with 1 M NaPF6 electrolyte displayed excellent cyclic stabilities at a wider temperature range of −20 to 50 °C (with the energy density of 151.48 Wh kg–1) due to the enhanced structural stability, alleviated Jahn–Teller distortions, and rapid Na+ kinetics facilitating Na+ motion at various temperatures in sodium-ion batteries. The detailed post-characterization studies revealed that the incorporation of LiF accounts for facile Na+ kinetics, boosting the overall Na storage."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03386/asset/images/acsami.3c03386.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da8a080f30b325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8a080f30b325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'e9e3abe7-ab72-450e-ac9c-2af4798d7347'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90da8a080f30b325-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8a080f30b325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90da8a080f30b325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Sustainable Enhanced Sodium-Ion Storage at Subzero Temperature with LiF Integration", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.3c03386", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D32291%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHeramba%2BVenkata%2BSai%2BRama%2BMurthy%2BKoppisetti%252C%2BHarsha%2BRao%252C%2BHari%2BVignesh%2BRamasamy%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D15%26issueNum%3D27%26contentID%3Dacsami.3c03386%26title%3DSustainable%2BEnhanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%2Bat%2BSubzero%2BTemperature%2Bwith%2BLiF%2BIntegration%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D32300%26publicationDate%3DJuly%2B2023" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03386/asset/images/medium/am3c03386_0009.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.3c03386/asset/images/large/am3c03386_0009.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.3c03386&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Though layered sodium oxide materials are identified as promising cathodes in sodium-ion batteries, biphasic P3/O3 depicts improved electrochemical performance and structural stability. Herein, a coexistent P3/O3 biphasic cathode material was synthesized with “LiF” integration, verified with X-ray diffraction and Rietveld refinement analysis. Furthermore, the presence of Li and F was deduced by inductively coupled plasma-optical emission spectrometry (ICP-OES) and energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS). The biphasic P3/O3 cathode displayed an excellent capacity retention of 85% after 100 cycles (0.2C/30 mA g<sup>–1</sup>) at room temperature and 94% at −20 °C after 100 cycles (0.1C/15 mA g<sup>–1</sup>) with superior rate capability as compared to the pristine cathode. Furthermore, a full cell comprising a hard carbon anode and a biphasic cathode with 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> electrolyte displayed excellent cyclic stabilities at a wider temperature range of −20 to 50 °C (with the energy density of 151.48 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup>) due to the enhanced structural stability, alleviated Jahn–Teller distortions, and rapid Na<sup>+</sup> kinetics facilitating Na<sup>+</sup> motion at various temperatures in sodium-ion batteries. The detailed post-characterization studies revealed that the incorporation of LiF accounts for facile Na<sup>+</sup> kinetics, boosting the overall Na storage.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D32291%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHeramba%2BVenkata%2BSai%2BRama%2BMurthy%2BKoppisetti%252C%2BHarsha%2BRao%252C%2BHari%2BVignesh%2BRamasamy%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D15%26issueNum%3D27%26contentID%3Dacsami.3c03386%26title%3DSustainable%2BEnhanced%2BSodium-Ion%2BStorage%2Bat%2BSubzero%2BTemperature%2Bwith%2BLiF%2BIntegration%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D32300%26publicationDate%3DJuly%2B2023" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2023 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Materials" class="article__tags__link">Materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290689&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Oxides" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Oxides" class="article__tags__link">Oxides</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291675&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Stability" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Stability" class="article__tags__link">Stability</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292316&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transition metals" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Transition%20metals" class="article__tags__link">Transition metals</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Lif+Incorporation&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_LiF%20incorporation">LiF incorporation</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium+Storage&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium%20storage">sodium storage</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Layered+Oxide&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_layered%20oxide">layered oxide</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Biphasic+Cathode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_biphasic%20cathode">biphasic cathode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Wide+Temperature&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_wide%20temperature">wide temperature</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The quest for efficient alternative energy storage systems is obligatory due to the intermittent nature of current energy storage systems such as lithium. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3" aria-label="reference 1 to 3">(1−3)</a> Earth-abundant sodium is considered as the next sodium-ion battery (SIB) technology not only for its lower cost but also for the ease of recyclability and enhanced extreme temperature performance compared to its lithium-ion counterparts. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 4 to 8">(4−8)</a> Designing novel host structures plays a pivotal role in developing high-performance SIBs with high capacity and longer cyclic stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9 ref10'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 9 and 10">(9,10)</a> Furthermore, considering the sustainable solar and wind storage in SIBs, it shall be operational at lower temperatures. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11 ref12'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 11 and 12">(11,12)</a> However, due to the larger size of the Na<sup>+</sup> (1.02 Å) ion, the extraction and insertion of the Na<sup>+</sup> ion during the charge and discharge processes result in structural changes, thus affecting the cyclic stability and rate performances of the cathode materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 13 and 14">(13,14)</a> Among the different reported cathode materials, layered transition-metal oxide (Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>TMO<sub>2</sub>; 0 &lt; <i>x</i> ≤ 1, TM––transition metal)-based materials are the state-of-the-art cathodes for SIBs, providing stable cycling and rate performance, incorporating large Na<sup>+</sup> (1.02 Å) during charge/discharge. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 15 and 16">(15,16)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">The layered oxides can be majorly classified into P2, P3, and O3 based on the coordination environment with the content of the alkali metal and the number of TMO<sub>2</sub> layers in the unit cell. In general, the P- and O-type structures represent prismatic and octahedral coordination around the Na ion, respectively. The adjoining numbers 2 and 3 indicate different arrangements of transition-metal layers in a single unit cell. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> Among these, P2- and O3- layered oxides are widely studied cathodes due to easy synthesis protocols like controlling the stoichiometry and reaction conditions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15" aria-label="reference 15">(15)</a> P2-type cathodes provide good rate capability and cycle life, whereas O3 delivers a higher initial capacity. However, all these layered structures suffer from multiple phase transitions and decreased capacity during long-term cycling. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18,19)</a> Consequently, it is highly desired to develop cathodes with optimized composition for improved cycle life and higher capacities. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> Several techniques like the integration of multiple phases and tuning the metal composition or incorporation of structure-stabilizing elements had already been proved to be very effective in improving the electrochemical performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20 ref21 ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22" aria-label="reference 20 to 22">(20−22)</a> For instance, Feng et al. explored the performance of a P2/O3 composite cathode (Na<sub>0.8</sub>Li<sub>0.13</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Fe<sub>0.1</sub>Mn<sub>0.57</sub>O<sub>2</sub>), which delivered a capacity of 133.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high rate of 1C and a capacity retention of 88.6% after 100 cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Additionally, the inexpensive, low-toxic manganese-based cathodes are highly advisable, but the Jahn–Teller distortion caused by the Mn<sup>3+</sup> ions results in the appearance of multiple voltage steps in the discharge curve, and the eventual capacity fade leads to further optimization of cathode compositions. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Recently, synergistic effects on biphasic cathodes which can be synthesized by controlling the reaction conditions, doping elements like Li, Mg, Al, Ti, Mn, Co, Fe, etc., have been demonstrated with improved electrochemical performance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25 ref26 ref27 ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref26 ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 25 to 28">(25−28)</a> An integrated P2/O3 Na<sub>0.66</sub>Li<sub>0.18</sub>Mn<sub>0.71</sub>Ni<sub>0.21</sub>Co<sub>0.08</sub>O<sub>2+δ</sub> cathode was reported by Guo et al., demonstrating superior sodium storage ability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> It is important to regulate the Mn valence to suppress the Jahn–Teller effect in layered manganese-based cathodes. Li inclusion into Mn-based layered oxide cathodes is reported to suppress the Jahn–Teller effect by regulating the Mn valence and delaying the phase transformations, resulting in prolonged cycling life. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> The substitution of Li can potentially help to suppress the Jahn–Teller effect by oxidizing Mn<sup>3+</sup> to Mn<sup>4+.</sup> A recent study by Li et al. with the Na<sub>0.95</sub>Li<sub>0.15</sub>Ni<sub>0.25</sub>Mn<sub>0.6</sub>0<sub>2</sub> cathode manifests improved electrochemical performance compared to the pristine material. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> Furthermore, Liu et al., using a Li/F codoping route, established a mixed P2/O3 cathode which possesses better electrochemical performance than the individual P2 and O3 phases. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> Fluorine substitution has been reported to be effective in addressing the oxygen loss issue in Na-based transition-metal oxides for improved cyclic stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33 ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 33 and 34">(33,34)</a> Additionally, doping with more electronegative F<sup>–</sup> ions accounts for stronger TM-O(F), which can minimize the gliding of the TMO<sub>2</sub> layers, thus making the layered structure more stable.</div><div class="NLM_p">Currently, major research on cathode materials is focused on ambient temperature, but very few reports are on SIB operable extreme conditions, specifically low temperature. The specific capacities and rate capabilities greatly reduce with the transition from room temperature to low temperatures due to the sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion processes at subzero temperatures. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref35" aria-label="reference 6 and 35">(6,35)</a> Wang et al. performed structural modifications to layered Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.33</sub>Mn<sub>0.67</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (specific capacity of 173 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2 C) by cobalt substitution, resulting in Na<sub>0.67</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.6</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, with 132.2 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> capacity at −40 ° C (80% retainment in the initial room-temperature capacity). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> A similar strategy with electrochemically active Fe<sup>3+</sup> ions in the Mn site of the P2 layer oxide cathode optimized as Na<sub>2/3</sub>Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>7/12</sub>Fe<sub>1/12</sub>O<sub>2</sub> exhibits a better low-temperature performance with a capacity retention of 94% after 80 cycles at −25 °C. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> Recently, lithium-composed layered oxide cathodes with stable structures have been employed at 0 °C for sodium storage. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> The strategic inclusion of foreign elements into layered oxide cathodes resulted in faster Na<sup>+</sup> transfer kinetics and ameliorated sodium storage properties at low temperatures. Therefore, it is highly envisaged to develop structurally stable and high-performance electrodes operable in extreme conditions, specifically subzero temperature.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, we have synthesized a new P3/O3 biphasic cathode by facile LiF codoping into Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as Na<sub>0.67</sub>Li<sub>0.07</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2–<i>x</i></sub>F<sub><i>x</i></sub> and Na<sub>0.67</sub>Li<sub>0.13</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2–<i>y</i></sub>F<sub><i>y</i></sub> through sol–gel synthesis, followed by a high-temperature calcination step. The LiF integration into Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> has led to the growth of a biphasic P3/O3 cathode, which is confirmed by XRD and Rietveld analyses. Moreover, the Jahn–Teller distortion from Mn<sup>3+</sup> is greatly suppressed with an increased Mn<sup>4+</sup>/Mn<sup>3+</sup> ratio, as confirmed by XPS analysis. At ambient temperature, the optimized cathode exhibits a capacity retention of ∼85% after 100 cycles at 0.2 C (30 mA g<sup>–1</sup>) rate compared to the 54% retention of the pristine cathode. Moreover, low-temperature performance at −20 °C gave 70% (92 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 C/15 mA g<sup>–1</sup>) of the room-temperature capacity, with 94% capacity retention after 100 cycles. Further, excellent capacity retention in a full-cell configuration, with hard carbon as an anode, has been demonstrated at a wider temperature range of −20 to 50 °C (with an energy density of 151.48 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup>). The Na<sup>+</sup> kinetic and postcharacterization studies reveal that the incorporation of LiF accounts for boosting the electrochemical performance.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4"> Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The chemicals sodium acetate and lithium fluoride are procured from Alfa Aesar, and anhydrous manganese(II) acetate and cobalt(II) acetate are obtained from Fisher Chemicals. Sodium hexafluorophosphate (NaPF<sub>6</sub>, Alfa Aesar) was dissolved in propylene carbonate (PC, Sigma) as the electrolyte.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5"> Synthesis of NMC and LiF-Incorporated NMC Cathode Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The Na<sub>0.67</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material was synthesized using a simple sol–gel method, followed by high-temperature calcination. Initially, stoichiometric amounts of metal (Na, Co, and Mn) acetates were dissolved in DI water along with citric acid and heated at 90 °C for 12 h to obtain a gel-like compound. Subsequently, the gel was dried at 120 °C to obtain the precursor material. Further, the precursor was sintered at 500 °C for 6 h. Finally, the precalcined material was further annealed at 800 °C for 15 h to obtain the final product. A similar procedure was used to obtain Li–F-incorporated samples Na<sub>0.67</sub>Li<sub>0.07</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2–<i>x</i></sub>F<sub><i>x</i></sub> and Na<sub>0.67</sub>Li<sub>0.13</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2–<i>y</i></sub>F<sub><i>y</i></sub> by additionally taking LiF in the first step, 10 and 20% moles of Na source were used for NMC-L1 and L2 samples, respectively. Both Na and Li precursors were taken in 5% excess quantity to account for the mass loss during high-temperature annealing. The obtained final products were used for further characterization.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Structural Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The elemental composition was determined using an inductively coupled plasma optical emission spectrometer. The PXRD patterns of the layered oxide cathodes were collected using a Rigaku Smart Lab X-ray diffractometer with a tube voltage of 40 kV and current of 44 mA. Cu Kα radiation source was used with a wavelength of 0.154 nm, and the scan range was set from 2-theta values of 10–70°. Further, for morphology analysis, an FEI Tecnai F20 S/transmission electron microscope and an FEI Nova NanoSEM field emission spectroscope were employed. XPS acquisition was done using a Kratos Axis ultra-DLD imaging XPS instrument. The XPS analysis was performed using CASA XPS fitting software, with the C 1s reference set at 284.6 eV and Shirley background. Majority of graphs were plotted using the Origin Pro 2022 software.</div></div><div id="sec2_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Electrochemical Testing</h3><div class="NLM_p">The active materials (80%), super P carbon (10%), and PVDF (10%) were taken with an appropriate amount of <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP) and mechanically mixed to obtain a uniform slurry. The slurry was further coated on the top of the aluminum current collector using the doctor blade technique and dried overnight at 100 °C in a vacuum oven. The dried foil was then punched into circular disks of diameter 12 mm with a mass loading of 2–3 mg cm<sup>–2</sup> and further used as cathodes. For the half-cells, the sodium metal foils rolled and cut into disks were used as anodes, and 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in propylene carbonate (PC) was used as the electrolyte, while glass microfiber filters (Whatman-grade GF/D) served as the separator. The full cells were assembled with hard carbon (Kuranode hard carbon powder, Kuraray). To prepare the negative carbon electrodes, a slurry of 80 wt % HC and 10 wt % each of super P carbon and PVDF in NMP was cast onto a copper current collector. The mass of the cathode and anode was taken in 10:8 ratio. CR 2032-type coin cells were subsequently assembled with the above components in an Ar-filled glovebox and tested with MTI and Arbin battery cyclers. The electrolyte composition remained unchanged for both room-temperature and low-temperature studies. The galvanostatic charge discharge (GCD) values of the electrodes were recorded in the potential range of 1.5–4.3 V at different specific currents of 0.1, 0.2 0.5, 1, 2, and 5C. The cycling studies were performed with the following C rate (1 C = 136 mA g<sup>–1</sup>) at various temperatures (0.2 C for RT, and 0.1 C for LT of −20 °C). Similarly, the cyclic voltammetry (CV) profiles were obtained in the same voltage window with varying scan rates of 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. The electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were recorded to measure the cell impedance in the range of 1 MHz–0.1 Hz with a voltage perturbation of 0.01 V.</div><div class="NLM_p last">The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients (<i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub>) are calculated according to the following equation:<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="ueq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-1"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-2"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-3"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-4"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-5"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-6" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-7">D</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-8" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-9"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-10" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-11">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-12" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-13">+</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-14"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-15" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-16"><span class="MJXp-mfrac" id="MJXp-Span-17" style="vertical-align: 0.25em;"><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-18"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-19">4</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-box" style="margin-top: -0.9em;"><span class="MJXp-denom"><span><span class="MJXp-rule" style="height: 1em;
