                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Designing high energy sodium-ion battery cathodes by utilizing P2/O3 biphasic structure and lithium honeycomb ordering</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Ji Eun; Kim, Heejin; Jung, Young Hwa; Kim, Do Kyung; Kim, Dong Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">30</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2100146</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides, in particular P2-type ones, are considered as promising cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries on account of their high specific capacity and rate capability.  Nevertheless, conventional layered compds. involve detrimental phase transformation throughout repeated cycles, which results in electrochem. performance degrdn.  Therefore, finding structurally stable layered compds., featuring minimal phase transition has been a key theme of the sodium-ion battery research.  Here lithium substituted Fe/Mn-based P2/O3 layered oxide-Na0.67Li0.2Fe0.2Mn0.6O2-that overcomes the inherited structural instability, is reported.  In situ synchrotron-based diffraction measurements and DFT calcns. are utilized, in order to identify the assocn. between P2/O3 biphasic structure and electrochem. performances.  The lithium honeycomb ordering within the P2/O3 biphasic layered compd. effectively constrains the undesirable phase transitions; more specifically, both P2-Z phase transition and Jahn-Teller distortion are suppressed throughout wide potential range of 1.5-4.5 V.  The DFT calcn. further discovers that the presence of honeycomb ordering is crucial for achieving the structural stability by forming Na-vac-Li and Na-Li-Na pairing at highly charged state.  The results highlight that the synergetic effect of P2/O3 biphasic structure and lithium substitution can provide an effective strategy toward achieving electrochem. stable layered cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGotoyq8UDQlmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljwz-tU4n79nQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVKmu7fI&amp;md5=4d8b4e127bb48d95a406a9d01afc0dbf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/cm5021788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceder, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis and Stoichiometry of Different Layered Sodium Cobalt Oxides</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and Stoichiometry of Different Layered Sodium Cobalt Oxides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lei, Yuechuan; Li, Xin; Liu, Lei; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5288-5296</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered Na-metal oxides can form in different crystal structures, each with different electrochem. behavior.  As a prototype system to better understand how each phase can be formed, we present the conditions under which different layered phases of NaxCoO2 can be stabilized in solid-state synthesis.  Using a novel combination of ex situ XRD on as-synthesized samples, with in situ XRD to monitor the relation between Na content and lattice parameters, we are able to construct a phase diagram of NaxCoO2 between 450 to 750 °C in air and for Na:Co sample ratios ranging from 0.60 to 1.05.  Four single phase domains of O3, O'3, P'3, and P2 are revealed based on the XRD anal.  In contrast to previous reports it is found that pure O3, O'3 and P'3 phase can only form at a fixed stoichiometry of x = 1.00, 0.83, and 0.67, resp., while the P2 phase forms in a slightly larger compn. range from 0.68 to 0.76.  Galvanostatic charging of O3-Na1.00CoO2 shows several flat and sloping regions on the voltage profile, which follows the sequence of O3-O'3-P'3-P3-P'3, with increasing interslab distances.  Our results indicate that the electrochem. important P2 structure is likely stabilized by entropy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrv-QfiXqid1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljwz-tU4n79nQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsVyjtL%252FI&amp;md5=da9f99c6485a2fb393272697bd36e7f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2020.04.040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, R.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient Method of Designing Stable Layered Cathode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries Using Aluminum Doping</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramasamy, Hari Vignesh; Kaliyappan, Karthikeyan; Thangavel, Ranjith; Seong, Won Mo; Kang, Kisuk; Chen, Zhongwei; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5021-5030</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCLCD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1948-7185</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite their high specific capacity, sodium layered oxides suffer from severe capacity fading when cycled at higher voltages.  This key issue must be addressed in order to develop high-performance cathodes for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we present a comprehensive study on the influence of Al doping of Mn sites on the structural and electrochem. properties of a P2-Na0.5Mn0.5-xAlxCo0.5O2 (x = 0, 0.02, or 0.05) cathode for SIBs.  Detailed structural, morphol., and electrochem. investigations were carried out using X-ray diffraction, cyclic voltammetry, and galvanostatic charge-discharge measurements, and some new insights are proposed.  Rietveld refinement confirmed that Al doping caused TMO6 octahedra (TM = transition metal) shrinkage, resulting in wider interlayer spacing.  After optimizing the aluminum concn., the cathode exhibited remarkable electrochem. performance, with better stability and improved rate performance.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were performed at various states of charge to probe the surface and bulk effects of Al doping.  The material presented here exhibits exceptional stability over 100 cycles within a 1.5-4.3 V window and outperforms several other Mn-Co-based cathodes for SIBs.  This study presents a facile method for designing structurally stable cathodes for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokIvkbRXYEObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljwz-tU4n79nQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel diphosphorus/ozone composite cathode toward synergistic electrochemical optimization for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Jiameng; Fang, De; Yang, Zhe; Zhong, Jianjian; Zheng, Chaoliang; Wei, Zhicheng; Li, Jianling</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">553</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">232292</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The P2-type and O3-type are the most common types of layered oxides.  The P2-type is possessed with better air stability but lower capacity while the O3-type possesses higher capacity but poorer kinetic performance.  Considering the complementarity of two phases, a series of P2/O3-Na0.80Li0.13Ni0.20FexMn0.67-xO2 (x = 0.05, 0.10, 0.15) are designed and successfully synthesized by Fe doping in this work.  The consolidation of P2 and O3 structures in this layered oxide is clearly characterized by the X-ray diffraction (XRD) refinement.  Surprisingly, the two-phase collaboration is well demonstrated in the superior electrochem. properties.  When x = 0.15, Fe0.15-LNM reveals a high reversible capacity with 180.95 mAh·g-1 and when x = 0.10, Fe0.10-LNM presents a good capacity retention with 88.60% after 100 cycles.  Here it is the O3-P3 reversible phase transition and the redox of Fe that mainly provide the capacity during sodium ion de-embedding.  Of note, the residual sodium salt on the surface is greatly reduced in the two-phase, which cuts down the occurrence of side reactions and improves the efficiency.  This novel composite phase strategy facilitates the design of promising cathode materials with high capacity and long lifetime for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and other alkali metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr5hZy9bAFrXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljwz-tU4n79nQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xislakur%252FE&amp;md5=447dd7e5e38d532a7978beb296f3ebd1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA06361B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hemalatha, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jayakumar, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bera, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prakash, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Incorporating nickel and magnesium into P2-Na0.67MnO2 is expected to suppress Jahn-Teller active Mn3+ ions, increase the av. potential of the electrode through Ni4+/Ni2+ redox couples and stabilize M-O layers resulting in a smooth cycling profile with better capacity retention.  In this communication, P2-Na0.67Ni0.25Mg0.1Mn0.65O2 is reported as the cathode material for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.  It reversibly intercalates ∼0.52 mol of Na per formula unit in the voltage region of 1.5-4.2 V at C/10 rate which corresponds to a specific capacity of 140 mA h/g.  XPS has attributed the origin of the capacity in this phase to both Ni and Mn redox species active at different potential ranges.  Substituting part of Mn with Ni and Mg increases the av. potential of Na0.67MnO2 and improves the energy d. of Na0.67Ni0.25Mg0.1Mn0.65O2 to 335 W h/kg.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpjvMoWmm8D3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liTfsv3NVQk6w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsF2ks7jE&amp;md5=61df7cb569408e57a1eddf56b679f7d6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501727"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Routes to High Energy Cathodes of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered Oxide Cathodes Promoted by Structure Modulation Technology for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Yao; Abbasi, Nasir Mahmood; Zhu, Yan-Fang; Li, Shi; Tan, Shuang-Jie; Ling, Wei; Peng, Ling; Yang, Tingqiang; Wang, Lude; Guo, Xiao-Dong; Yin, Ya-Xia; Zhang, Han; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Considering the ever-growing climatic degeneration, sustainable and renewable energy sources are needed to be effectively integrated into the grid through large-scale electrochem. energy storage and conversion (EESC) technologies.  With regard to their competent benefit in cost and sustainable supply of resource, room-temp. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have shown great promise in EESC, triumphing over other battery systems on the market.  As one of the most fascinating cathode materials due to the simple synthesis process, large specific capacity, and high ionic cond., Na-based layered transition metal oxide cathodes commonly suffer from the sluggish kinetics, multiphase evolution, poor air stability, and insufficient comprehensive performance, restricting their commercialization application.  Here, this review summarizes the recent advances in layered oxide cathode materials for SIBs through different optimal structure modulation technologies, with an emphasis placed on strategies to boost Na+ kinetics and reduce the irreversible phase transition as well as enhance the store stability.  Meanwhile, a thorough and in-depth systematical investigation of the structure-function-property relationship is also discussed, and the challenges as well as opportunities for practical application electrode materials are sketched.  The insights brought forward in this review can be considered as a guide for SIBs in next-generation EESC.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIp2jAl8Fi6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liTfsv3NVQk6w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXotlSmt70%253D&amp;md5=7e725324572425310bb9bcb4e649eca0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of intergrown P/O-type biphasic layered oxides as high-performance cathodes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Kai; Wu, Zhen-Guo; Melinte, Georgian; Yang, Zu-Guang; Sarkar, Abhishek; Hua, Weibo; Mu, Xiaoke; Yin, Zu-Wei; Li, Jun-Tao; Guo, Xiao-Dong; Zhong, Ben-He; Kubel, Christian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This study reports on the solid-state synthesis and characterization of novel quaternary P/O intergrown biphasic Na0.8MnyNi0.8-yFe0.1Ti0.1O2 (y = 0.6, 0.55, 0.5, 0.45) cathode materials.  Electrochem. tests reveal superior performance of the P/O biphasic materials in a sodium ion battery compared to the single P2 or O3 phases, proving the beneficial effect of the intergrowth of P2 and O3 materials.  The nature of the P/O interface was studied by transmission electron microscopy.  The anal. shows a semi-coherent interface grown along the a/b and c axes with local differences in the transition metal concn. along the interface between the two phases.  EDX and EELS characterization revealed a charge compensation mechanism across the phase boundary based on variation of the transition element distribution, balancing the different sodium contents in the P and O phases.  The results reported in this study provide a better understanding of P/O biphasic materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrq_bzYfQ22vbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liTfsv3NVQk6w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtVeqsrnK&amp;md5=0bc61ab0db769146a1cfe2d5835641d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201411788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishida, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Layered P2- and O3-Type Composite as a High-Energy Cathode for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improving Energy Density and Structural Stability of Manganese Oxide Cathodes for Na-Ion Batteries by Structural Lithium Substitution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">de la Llave, Ezequiel; Talaie, Elahe; Levi, Elena; Nayak, Prasant Kumar; Dixit, Mudit; Rao, Penki Tirupathi; Hartmann, Pascal; Chesneau, Frederick; Major, Dan Thomas; Greenstein, Miri; Aurbach, Doron; Nazar, Linda F.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report excellent cycling performance for P2-Na0.6Li0.2Mn0.8O2, an auspicious cathode material for Na-ion batteries.  This oxide, which comprises mainly Mn4+, exhibits a long voltage plateau on the 1st charge that is similar to that of high-capacity Li and Mn-rich metal oxides.  Electrochem. measurements, x-ray diffraction, and elemental anal. of the cycled electrodes suggest an activation process that includes the extn. of Li from the material.  The activated material delivers a high specific capacity of ∼160 mAh/g on the 1st discharge and 190 mAh/g over &gt; 100 cycles, when cycled between 4.6 - 2.0 V vs. Na/Na+.  DFT calcns. locate the energy states of O atoms near the Fermi level, suggesting the contribution of O electrochem. to the redox process.  The addn. of Li in the lattice stabilizes the structure compared to many previously reported sodiated transition metal oxide electrode materials, by inhibiting detrimental structural transformations during cycling.  This research demonstrates the prospect of intercalation materials that are active based on both cationic and anionic redox for Na-ion battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqPTxGUC8CQG7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLZESZm1qjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslOhsrvE&amp;md5=3e97a5f1df8ff8627ce0a904a0dbe574</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.136923"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of Lithium Doping in P2-Type Layered Oxide Cathodes on the Electrochemical Performances of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of lithium doping in P2-Type layered oxide cathodes on the electrochemical performances of Sodium-Ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Lijiang; Su, Gaoqin; Lu, Chu; Ma, Xiaobo; Ma, Ling; Wang, Hailong; Cao, Zhijie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anionic redox reaction offers an effective way to design high-performance cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Here to trigger the lattice oxygen redox reaction, the effect of Li doping on the electrochem. performances of P2-type layered oxide cathodes are systematically investigated.  Results show that the introduction of Li can not only induce oxygen anions to participate in the charge compensation under high operating voltage, but also suppress the unfavorable P2-O2 transition and facilitate the diffusion of Na+ and electrons during the sodiation/desodiation process.  Therefore, Li-doped layered oxide cathodes show improved electrochem. performances with higher reversible capacity, better rate capability, and longer cycling stability.  This study may provide a ref. point for designing advanced cathode materials through activating the anionic redox reaction.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGozR-ZIOJcE1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLZESZm1qjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtlWltL3J&amp;md5=6e5a834d990e82340d9b0fbd1ec42cf3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.134273"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phase Tuning of P2/O3-Type Layered Oxide Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries via a Simple Li/F Co-Doping Route</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase tuning of P2/O3-type layered oxide cathode for sodium ion batteries via a simple Li/F co-doping route</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhengbo; Zhou, Chaojin; Liu, Jun; Yang, Lichun; Liu, Jiangwen; Zhu, Min</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Element doping is a common and effective method for improving the electrochem. performance of cathode materials, and typically it can be divided into cation ion and anion ion doping.  Among the cathode materials of sodium-ion batteries, the important layered oxide cathodes mainly include those of O3 and P2 types, according to the sites of Na ions and the no. of oxide layer packings.  Hereon, the successful transformation of O3-type cathode NaNi0.45Mn0.4Ti0.1Co0.05O2 (O3-NMTCO) into P2-type cathode of NaNi0.45Mn0.4Ti0.1Co0.05O2-0.08LiF (P2-LNMTCOF) is achieved via a facile Li/F co-doping route.  The modified P2-type cathode (P2-LNMTCOF) have main three advantages over the traditional P2-type cathode Na0.7Ni0.45Mn0.4Ti0.1Co0.05O2 (P2-NMTCO): higher Na content, solid soln. reaction in high-voltage range, and stronger TM-F bond.  As a result, the current P2-LNMTCOF cathode shows the best cycling performance, with the initial capacity of about 160 mA h g-1 and the capacity retention of 61% after 200 cycles.  In addn., because of the more stable TM-O (F) octahedron, the voltage drop during cycling has been effectively suppressed.  This study provides a new idea and ref. for synthesizing high performance P2-type layered oxide cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpkSIa8GbxzR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLZESZm1qjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisVeqsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=90465e47162ff8f572e63e48bfcfd870</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.2c03391"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ganesan, B.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase Transition Induced Enhanced Performance of Sodium-Rich Na1.2Mn0.8O2-yFy (y = 0-0.5) Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ganesan, Bala Krishnan; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Increasing capacity and cycle stability is key to successfully commercializing sodium battery technologies.  Currently, cation-rich cathodes are well suited for this trend owing to superior overall performance through fluorine substitution in the cation.  However, the exact effects and synergy due to fluorine substitution as anions are still unknown.  Understanding such synergistic effects can significantly facilitate increasing the capacity, leading to max. performance at optimum conditions.  In this work, the systematic addn. of F into sodium-layered oxide and its corresponding changes in the crystal structure or phase formation are extensively studied.  More specifically, the effect of fluorine substitution in the anion site on Na diffusion and the Na-Tm polyhedral are extensively studied using X-ray diffraction and subsequent Rietveld anal.  In addn., the effects of F on transition metals (i.e., Mn) and its valence states are also analyzed using X-ray absorption spectroscopy.  Na1.2Mn0.8O1.5F0.5 not only showed superior capacity of approx. 172 mA h g-1 and capacity retention but also remarkable cycling stability for up to 300 cycles at higher current densities.  Improvements in the performance due to distortion induced by F substitution are also presented.         (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">139876</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Among the various sodium cathodes, the potential of Na-rich layered oxides is yet to be fully utilized.  Unlike their Li counterparts, they are least explored and are at least a generation behind in development.  Addressing the same, herein, Na-rich NaxMn2-xO1.5F0.5 (x = 1.05-1.3) type cathodes were synthesized successfully and analyzed as potential electrodes for Na-ion battery applications.  Oxygen loss in Na-based transition metal oxides is a common issue, and it is effectively addressed by fluorine substitution.  In contrast to exploring a particular stoichiometry as in other Na-deficient layered cathodes, herein, Na-content was gradually increased from 1.05 to 1.3.  The cathodes were synthesized using a conventional solid-state approach and quenched to achieve high crystallinity.  Compds. with different sodium stoichiometry were electrochem. tested in a half-cell configuration.  Among these compds., the Na1.2Mn0.8O1.5F0.5 electrode exhibited very high capacities of 178 and 122 mAhg-1 at current densities of 10 and 1000 mA g-1, resp.  The Na-rich Na1.2Mn0.8O1.5F0.5 cathode was systematically analyzed to understand the mechanism underlying its superior performance using various structural and electrochem. analyses.  Furthermore, to demonstrate its practicality, the Na-rich Na1.2Mn0.8O1.5F0.5 cathode was coupled with a hard carbon and Na-In alloy anode in a full-cell assembly.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpIXUy5K9bb_LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgpLZESZm1qjQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XivVSgsb7L&amp;md5=76e26f9ebaba8debe139e1c221a4caeb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-022-32606-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thenuwara, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nonaq. sodium-based batteries are ideal candidates for the next generation of electrochem. energy storage devices.  However, despite the promising performance at ambient temp., their low-temp. (e.g., &lt; 0°C) operation is detrimentally affected by the increase in the electrolyte resistance and solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) instability.  Here, to circumvent these issues, we propose specific electrolyte formulations comprising linear and cyclic ether-based solvents and sodium trifluoromethanesulfonate salt that are thermally stable down to -150°C and enable the formation of a stable SEI at low temps.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design of Na0.67Ni0.2Co0.2Mn0.6O2 microsphere cathode material for stable and low temperature sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xuan; Yin, Xiuping; Feng, Xiaochen; Li, Yong; Dong, Xiping; Shi, Qinhao; Zhao, Yufeng; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides with a classic compn. of Na0.67Ni0.33Mn0.67O2 have attracted extensive attention due to their high specific capacity and suitable working voltage.  In this work, a suitable Co-substituted Na0.67Ni0.2Co0.2Mn0.6O2 microsphere is designed and synthesized.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn7/12Fe1/12O2 Cathode Material with Suppressed P2-O2 Phase Transition toward High-Performance Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Qiong; Wang, Peng-Fei; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Chen, Zi-Ming; Pang, Wei-Lin; Huang, Ke-Cheng; Guo, Yu-Guo; Wu, Xing-Long; Zhang, Jing-Ping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As a promising cathode material of sodium-ion battery, P2-type Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 (NNMO) possesses a theor. high capacity and working voltage to realize high energy storage d.  However, it still suffers from poor cycling stability mainly incurred by the undesirable P2-O2 phase transition.  Herein, the electrochem. active Fe3+ ions are introduced into the lattice of NNMO, forming Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3-xFexO2 (x = 0, 1/24, 1/12, 1/8, 1/6) to effectively stabilize the P2-type cryst. structure.  In such Fe-substituted materials, both Ni2+/Ni4+ and Fe3+/Fe4+ couples take part in the redox reactions, and the P2-O2 phase transition is well restrained during cycling, as verified by ex situ X-ray diffraction.  As a result, the optimized Na2/3Ni1/3Mn7/12Fe1/12O2 (1/12-NNMF) has a long-term cycling stability with the fading rate of 0.05% per cycle over 300 cycles at 5 C.  Furthermore, the 1/12-NNMF delivers excellent rate capabilities (65 mA h g-1 at 25 C) and superior low-temp. performance (the capacity retention of 94% at -25° after 80 cycles) owing to the enhanced Na diffusion upon Fe doping, which is deduced by the studies of electrode kinetics.  More significantly, the 1/12-NNMF also displays remarkable sodium-ion full-cell properties when merged with an LS-Sb@G anode, thus implying the possibility of their practical application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGogYDHbEbm6hLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjxM9WYk3hbA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P3/O3 Integrated Layered Oxide as High-Power and Long-Life Cathode toward Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Si-Yuan; Guo, Yu-Jie; Zhou, Ya-Nan; Zhang, Xu-Dong; Niu, Yu-Bin; Wang, En-Hui; Huang, Lin-Bo; An, Peng-Fei; Zhang, Jing; Yang, Xin-An; Yin, Ya-Xia; Xu, Sailong; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Low-cost and stable sodium-layered oxides (such as P2- and O3-phases) are suggested as highly promising cathode materials for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Biphasic hybridization, mainly involving P2/O3 and P2/P3 biphases, is typically used to boost their electrochem. performances.  Herein, a P3/O3 intergrown layered oxide (Na2/3Ni1/3Mn1/3Ti1/3O2) as high-rate and long-life cathode for NIBs via tuning the amts. of Ti substitution in Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3-xTixO2 (x = 0, 1/6, 1/3, 2/3) is demonstrated.  The X-ray diffraction (XRD) Rietveld refinement and aberration-cor. scanning transmission electron microscopy show the co-existence of P3 and O3 phases, and d. functional theory calcn. corroborates the appearance of the anomalous O3 phase at the Ti substitution amt. of 1/3.  The P3/O3 biphasic cathode delivers an unexpected rate capability (≈88.7% of the initial capacity at a high rate of 5 C) and cycling stability (≈68.7% capacity retention after 2000 cycles at 1 C), superior to those of the sing phases P3-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2, P3-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn1/2Ti1/6O2, and O3-Na2/3Ni1/3Ti2/3O2.  The highly reversible structural evolution of the P3/O3 integrated cathode obsd. by ex situ XRD, ex situ X-ray absorption spectra, and the rapid Na+ diffusion kinetics, underpin the enhancement.  These results show the important role of P3/O3 biphasic hybridization in designing and engineering layered oxide cathodes for NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrT3qth0NlKw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjxM9WYk3hbA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktVOhuro%253D&amp;md5=1f6f6716c7d00cc77972c05b64e7f2ed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201400458"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miller, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">DeWahl, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hackney, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Key, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Slater, M.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li-Substituted Co-Free Layered P2/O3 Biphasic Na0.67Mn0.55Ni0.25Ti0.2-xLixO2 as High-Rate-Capability Cathode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zheng-Yao; Zhang, Jicheng; Gao, Rui; Zhang, Heng; Zheng, Lirong; Hu, Zhongbo; Liu, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">120</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9007-9016</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The effects of Li substitution for Ti on the structure and electrochem. performances of Co-free Na0.67Mn0.55Ni0.25Ti0.2-xLixO2 (x = 0, 0.1, 0.2) layered cathode materials for sodium ion batteries were comprehensively investigated.  X-ray diffraction and Rietveld refinement results demonstrate that Li mainly occupies TM (TM = transition metal) sites in the crystal structure to maintain the P2 structure majority and a small amt. of Li atoms enter Na sites to generate some O3 phase.  The discharge voltage, reversible capacity, rate capability, cycling performance, and Coulombic efficiency all were improved by Li substitution, which can be largely attributed to the integration of P2 and O3.  Li substitution also raises the av. discharge voltage from 2.6-3.1 V.  Na0.67Mn0.55Ni0.25Li0.2O2 (L02) can deliver an initial capacity of about 158 mA h g-1 at 0.05C (12 mA g-1) in comparison with the Li-free sample (147 mA h g-1).  Even at the high rates of 480 (2C), 1200 (5C), and 1920 (8C) mA g-1, L02 can also display ca. 93, 65, and 38 mA h g-1 discharge capacities, resp.  The rate capability is higher than what is reported in the previous Li-substituted cathode materials.  In addn., Li substitution in transition-metal sites generates more defects to maintain the charge neutrality, which enhances the electronic cond. and also has a pos. effect on the Na ion diffusion coeff.  The electronic cond. and Na ion diffusion coeff. have been enhanced by 122% and 29%, resp., with the substitution of Li for Ti.  Our results also show that the oxidn. peaks become sharper with increasing Li content, which indicates the feasibility of Na ion intercalation/deintercalation in the integrated P2/O3 phase.  This study also offers some new insights into designing high-performance cathode materials for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq3vX_u19Wr3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjxM9WYk3hbA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XlvVyqsr8%253D&amp;md5=e98713315bb6626e0cd01b06d597782d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/C4CP02957G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct imaging of layered O3- and P2-NaxFe1/2Mn1/2O2 structures at the atomic scale</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Xia; Wang, Yuesheng; Liu, Pin; Gu, Lin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Demopoulos, George P.; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Using aberration-cor. scanning TEM (STEM) with high-angle annular-dark-field (HAADF) and annular-bright-field (ABF) techniques, the at.-scale structures of the O3 and P2 phases of NaxFe1/2Mn1/2O2 were studied systematically.  The Na, transition metal M (Fe and Mn) and O columns are well revealed and precisely assigned to the O3 and P2 phase layered structures.  The O3 phase sample demonstrates larger at. site fluctuations along [001] direction but with less structural imperfections (e.g. interlayer structure and stacking defaults) than the P2 phase sample.  Also, a clear surface with a regular structure is obsd. for the O3-NaFe1/2Mn1/2O2 sample, while a surface with a large amt. of Na-M antisites is obsd. for the P2-Na2/3Fe1/2Mn1/2O2 sample.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrbCVagdwBB6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljyw53USIU5IQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsVaks7bN&amp;md5=0d86bd63533af561831adf5aba71f596</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/D0DT03351K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stansby, J.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biphasic P2/O3-Na2/3Li0.18Mn0.8Fe0.2O2: a structural investigation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Stansby, Jennifer H.; Avdeev, Maxim; Brand, Helen E. A.; Gonzalo, Elena; Drewett, Nicholas E.; Ortiz-Vitoriano, Nagore; Sharma, Neeraj; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The P2/O3 layered oxide system is thought to benefit from a synergistic enhancement, resulting from the presence of both phases, which makes it a promising cathode material for Na-ion battery applications.  Here, biphasic P2/O3-Na2/3Li0.18Mn0.8Fe0.2O2 is investigated via a combination of neutron and X-ray scattering techniques.  Neutron diffraction data indicates that the O3 alkali metal site is fully occupied by Li.  Real time operando X-ray diffraction data shows the structural evolution of the composite electrode - at the charged state there is no evidence of O2, OP4 or Z phases.  The results presented herein provide new insight into site preference of Li in biphasic materials and highlights the value of utilizing multiple phases to achieve high performance layered cathode materials for sodium battery applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqkWbV_RtGlwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljyw53USIU5IQ"> &gt;&gt; Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1062</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1067</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mitigation of Jahn-Teller distortion and Na+/vacancy ordering in a distorted manganese oxide cathode material by Li substitution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yanchen; Wang, Chenchen; Zhao, Shuo; Zhang, Lin; Zhang, Kai; Li, Fujun; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1062-1067</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSHCCN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-6520</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered manganese-based oxides are promising candidates as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their low cost and high specific capacity.  However, the Jahn-Teller distortion from high-spin Mn3+ induces detrimental lattice strain and severe structural degrdn. during sodiation and desodiation.  Herein, lithium is introduced to partially substitute manganese ions to form distorted P'2-Na0.67Li0.05Mn0.95O2, which leads to restrained anisotropic change of Mn-O bond lengths and reinforced bond strength in the [MnO6] octahedra by mitigation of Jahn-Teller distortion and contraction of MnO2 layers.  This ensures the structural stability during charge and discharge of P'2-Na0.67Li0.05Mn0.95O2 and Na+/vacancy disordering for facile Na+ diffusion in the Na layers with a low activation energy barrier of ~ 0.53 eV.  It exhibits a high specific capacity of 192.2 mA h g-1, good cycling stability (90.3% capacity retention after 100 cycles) and superior rate capability (118.5 mA h g-1 at 1.0 A g-1), as well as smooth charge/discharge profiles.  This strategy is effective to tune the crystal structure of layered oxide cathodes for SIBs with high performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1zwIYbYy0qLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljyw53USIU5IQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitlWktbfP&amp;md5=cbf302cbfea31e944b525db909d4e1dc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.jelechem.2023.117222"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ramesh, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tripathi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bosman, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Balaya, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhancement in Rate Performance and High Voltage Structural Stability of P3/O3 Na<sub>0.9</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.45</sub>Ni<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Layered Oxide Cathode</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancement in rate performance and high voltage structural stability of P3/O3 Na0.9Fe0.5Mn0.45Ni0.05O2 layered oxide cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramesh, Aniruddh; Tripathi, Abhinav; Bosman, Michel; Xi, Shibo; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electroanalytical Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">932</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">117222</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report synthesis and Na storage performances of two biphasic P3/O3 materials, Na0.9Fe0.5Mn0.5O2 (P3/O3 NFM) and Na0.9Fe0.5Mn0.45Ni0.05O2 (P3/O3 NFNM).  The choice of compn. and Ni doping context were justified.  On replacing 5% Mn by Ni, the authors found improvements in (de)sodiation capacity and rate performance.  The delivered storage capacities of P3/O3 NFM and P3/O3 NFNM in the 1st cycle between 4.4 and 2.0 V are 118 mAh g-1 and 148 mAh g-1 at C/10 (0.015Ag-1) rate, resp.  The subsequent cycles have a narrow voltage window of 4.2 to 1.9 V for optimized cycling performance.  In this voltage window, P3/O3 NFNM demonstrates more than twice the discharge capacity of P3/O3 NFM at 3C rate (0.45Ag-1); further it retains 74% of its capacity after 200 cycles at 1C rate (0.15Ag-1) as compared to 57% in P3/O3 NFM.  X-ray diffraction studies confirm that Ni doping helps in retaining the P3 phase throughout the charge cycle in P3/O3 NFNM which helps in achieving a higher discharge capacity and better cycling.  A greater redn. in the internal resistance, specifically the charge transfer resistance along with enhanced hole cond. is obsd. from impedance studies of fully desodiated P3/O3 NFNM due to the maintenance of the P3 phase.  XANES studies reveal that the charge compensation mechanism of Fe and Mn changes upon Ni doping which is attributed to the structural stability of P3/O3 NFNM at higher voltages.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrhW1oMe4Z7S7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZ3U5WxkNUQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3sXislyhsr0%253D&amp;md5=24d2afbb3156ef6ad8968bdb6da65878</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/cm702546s"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahéron, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dedryvère, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Martinez, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ménétrier, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Denage, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Delmas, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gonbeau, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electron Transfer Mechanisms upon Lithium Deintercalation from LiCoO<sub>2</sub> to CoO<sub>2</sub> Investigated by XPS</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electron Transfer Mechanisms upon Lithium Deintercalation from LiCoO2 to CoO2 Investigated by XPS</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Daheron, L.; Dedryvere, R.; Martinez, H.; Menetrier, M.; Denage, C.; Delmas, C.; Gonbeau, D.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">583-590</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li deintercalation of LixCoO2 from x = 1 to x ≈ 0 was carried out electrochem.  The changes in the electronic structure from LiCoO2 to CoO2 were studied by XPS to bring some new developments about the electron transfer mechanisms upon Li deintercalation.  All available XPS core peaks (Co 2p, Co 3p, Co 3s, O 1s, F 1s, P 2p, C 1s) and valence spectra were analyzed.  The contributions of the electrode material and of the electrode/electrolyte interface were clearly distinguished.  Co and O simultaneously undergo a partial oxidn. process and the sole participation of O atoms to the charge transfer process, as it is sometimes assumed, can be excluded.  The surface film consists of org. and inorg. species resulting from degrdn. of the electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoITAtbm4ocMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZ3U5WxkNUQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXhsVemtrvL&amp;md5=950d521ba17e806d7a5140fa51101c58</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.2c00497"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ghosh, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mondal, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tudu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ghosh, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Koppisetti, H.                 10.1021/acssuschemeng.2c00497</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D7265-7276%26journal%3DACS%2BSustainable%2BChem.%2BEng.%26author%3DS.%2BGhosh%26author%3DA.%2BMondal%26author%3DG.%2BTudu%26author%3DS.%2BGhosh%26author%3DH.%2BV.%2BS.%2BR.%2BM.%2BKoppisetti%26author%3DH.%2BR.%2BInta%26author%3DD.%2BSaha%26author%3DV.%2BMahalingam%26title%3DEfficient%2BElectrochemical%2BReconstruction%2Bof%2Ba%2BCobalt-%2Band%2BSilver-Based%2BPrecatalytic%2BOxalate%2BFramework%2Bfor%2BBoosting%2Bthe%2BAlkaline%2BWater%2BOxidation%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facssuschemeng.2c00497&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03386&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facssuschemeng.2c00497&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient Electrochemical Reconstruction of a Cobalt- and Silver-Based Precatalytic Oxalate Framework for Boosting the Alkaline Water Oxidation Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ghosh, Suptish; Mondal, Ayan; Tudu, Gouri; Ghosh, Sourav; Koppisetti, Heramba V. S. R. M.; Inta, Harish Reddy; Saha, Dipannita; Mahalingam, Venkataramanan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7265-7276</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASCECG</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The quest toward finding an efficient oxygen evolution reaction (OER) catalyst utilizing a sustainable and facile synthetic strategy is still underway.  Low overpotential, better stability, and rapid kinetics are the key features to be considered while designing a competent OER catalyst.  Herein, we have developed a rapid and efficient wet chem. route for the synthesis of a cobalt- and silver- based precatalytic oxalate (CoC2O4/Ag2C2O4) framework via a rapid pptn. method at room temp.  The optimized catalyst required an overpotential of 260 mV to reach the benchmark c.d. of 10 mA/cm2geo, with a Tafel slope value of 47 mV/dec.  It has also shown 72 h of chronopotentiometry stability as well as 1000 cycles of potentiodynamic stability along with 90% Faradaic efficiency in 1(M) KOH for OER.  Addn. of a minimal amt. of silver component assists in the redn. of overpotential up to 120 mV compared to CoC2O4.  Furthermore, the minimal amt. of silver inclusion improved the charge migration property via lowering the charge-transfer resistance besides tuning the charge storage mechanism (b value).  The paradigm shift in catalytic efficiency can be manifested by calcg. both intrinsic (per-site activity) and geometric (based on the effective area of electrode materials) activities.  Interestingly, significant improvement in Cdl (double-layer capacitance) from 10.25 to 19.59 mF/cm2 is achieved upon silver component inclusion, indicating a higher no. of accessible catalytic sites for alk. OER.  The turnover frequency value further authenticates the importance of silver component in the precatalytic oxalate network for intrinsic catalytic activity under alk. conditions.  The mechanistic trajectory is also investigated from the proton reaction order (ρRHE), revealing the occurrence of the proton-decoupled electron transfer process for the optimized catalyst.  The results reveal the efficient electrochem. surface reconstruction in the cobalt- and silver-based precatalytic oxalate framework for improved alk. water oxidn. through exposing the surface as well as bulk active centers for easy electrolyte diffusion in alk. medium.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpDW66oJUSDQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZ3U5WxkNUQw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xhtlaltr7K&amp;md5=0d31cdb60be76ff39b005a295cfefe22</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b00614"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cu2+ Dual-Doped Layer-Tunnel Hybrid Na0.6Mn1-xCuxO2 as a Cathode of Sodium-Ion Battery with Enhanced Structure Stability, Electrochemical Property, and Air Stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Ting-Ru; Sheng, Tian; Wu, Zhen-Guo; Li, Jun-Tao; Wang, En-Hui; Wu, Chun-Jin; Li, Hong-Tai; Guo, Xiao-Dong; Zhong, Ben-He; Huang, Ling; Sun, Shi-Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10147-10156</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been regarded as a promising candidate for large-scale renewable energy storage system.  Layered Mn oxide cathode possesses the advantages of high energy d., low cost and natural abundance while suffering from limited cycling life and poor rate capacity.  To overcome these weaknesses, layer-tunnel hybrid material was developed and served as the cathode of SIB, which integrated high capacity, superior cycle ability, and rate performance.  Here, the doping of Cu was adopted to suppress the Jahn-Teller effect of Mn3+ and to affect relevant structural parameters.  Multifunctions of the Cu2+ doping were studied.  It was found that the structure component ratio is varied with the Cu2+ doping amt.  Results demonstrated that Na+/vacancy rearrangement and phase transitions were suppressed during cycling without sacrificing the reversible capacity and enhanced electrochem. performances evidenced with 96 mAh/g retained after 250 cycles at 4 C and 85 mAh/g at 8 C.  Ex situ x-ray diffraction has demonstrated high reversibility of the Na0.6Mn0.9Cu0.1O2 cathode during Na+ extn./insertion processes and superior air stability that results in better storage properties.  This study reveals that the Cu2+ doping could be an effective strategy to tune the properties and related performances of Mn-based layer-tunnel hybrid cathode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDlw2Tmt_qsbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgZ3U5WxkNUQw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Influence of the manganese and cobalt content on the electrochemical performance of P2-Na0.67MnxCo1-xO2 cathodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hemalatha, K.; Jayakumar, M.; Prakash, A. S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">47</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1223-1232</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The resurgence of sodium-ion batteries in recent years is due to their potential ability to form intercalation compds. possessing a high specific capacity and energy d. comparable to existing lithium systems.  To comprehend the role of cobalt substitution in the structure and electrochem. performance of Na0.67MnO2, the solid solns. of P2-Na0.67MnxCo1-xO2 (x = 0.25, 0.5, 0.75) are synthesized and characterized.  The XRD-Rietveld anal. revealed that the Co-substitution in Na0.67MnO2 decreases lattice parameters 'a' and 'c' resulting in the contraction of MO6 octahedra and the enlargement of inter-layer 'd' spacing.  XPS indicates that the isovalent cobalt substitution in Na0.67MnO2 results in the partial/complete replacement of Jahn-Teller active trivalent manganese to form low-spin complexes of better structural stability.  The Na-ion diffusion coeff., DNa+, derived from cyclic voltammetry and impedance spectroscopy, confirmed the enhanced mass transport in Co-rich phases compared to Mn-rich phases.  Furthermore, higher diffusion coeff. values are obsd. for Co3+/Co4+ than for their Mn3+/Mn4+ redox processes.  In addn., Co-rich phases exhibit a high structural stability and superior capacity retention, whereas Mn-rich phases discharge higher capacities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRS1d1iefuWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgucN6DXF787A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvFyhurfM&amp;md5=34faff33fb3517a9547609f723dff18f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA02450A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Designing an Advanced P2-Na<sub>0.67</sub>Mn<sub>0.65</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Co<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Layered Cathode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">16272</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">16278</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5TA02450A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D16272-16278%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DZ.%2BY.%2BLi%26author%3DR.%2BGao%26author%3DL.%2BSun%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26title%3DDesigning%2Ban%2BAdvanced%2BP2-Na0.67Mn0.65Ni0.2Co0.15O2%2BLayered%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC5TA02450A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03386&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5TA02450A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Designing an advanced P2-Na0.67Mn0.65Ni0.2Co0.15O2 layered cathode material for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zheng-Yao; Gao, Rui; Sun, Limei; Hu, Zhongbo; Liu, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">31</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16272-16278</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A high performance layered P2-Na0.67Mn0.65Ni0.2Co0.15O2 cathode material for sodium ion batteries with high rate capability and excellent long-life cyclic performance has been successfully designed and synthesized by a simple sol-gel method.  In comparison with the reported Na0.7MnO2, the designed P2-Na0.67Mn0.65Ni0.2Co0.15O2 cathode material can be charged and discharged in an extended voltage range of 1.5-4.2 V and shows reversible capacities of 155, 144, 137, 132, and 126 mA h g-1 at different current densities of 12, 24, 48, 120, and 240 mA g-1, resp.  Even at high current densities of 480 (2C), 1200 (5C) and 1920 mA g-1 (8C) it can still deliver capacities of 117, 93 and 70 mA h g-1, resp., which are much higher than those of the recently reported Na0.5[Ni0.23Fe0.13Mn0.63]O2.  In addn., the Na0.67Mn0.65Ni0.2Co0.15O2 cathode material also displays an excellent capacity retention ca. 85 and 78% after 100 cycles at 0.05C and 0.5C, resp.  It is also proposed that Mn4+ may be activated in a low voltage range, esp. below 2.0 V, which contributes to the addnl. capacity.  The Na-ion diffusion coeff., DNa+, is ca. 10-14 cm2 s-1 as calcd. by the PITT and the discharge diffusion coeff. is a little larger than the charge one.  The designed Na0.67Mn0.65Ni0.2Co0.15O2 shows great potential as a cathode material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9luVkngv86LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgucN6DXF787A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWmtbzI&amp;md5=bc91f44110fe7f6aeaf60a5eb89bdc32</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2019.12.132"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ramasamy, H. Colloid Interface Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>564</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">467</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">477</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jcis.2019.12.132</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D564%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D467-477%26journal%3DJ.%2BColloid%2BInterface%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BV.%2BRamasamy%26author%3DP.%2BN.%2BDidwal%26author%3DS.%2BSinha%26author%3DV.%2BAravindan%26author%3DJ.%2BHeo%26author%3DC.-J.%2BPark%26author%3DY.-S.%2BLee%26title%3DAtomic%2BLayer%2BDeposition%2Bof%2BAl2O3%2Bon%2BP2-Na0.5Mn0.5Co0.5O2%2Bas%2BInterfacial%2BLayer%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BPower%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jcis.2019.12.132&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.3c03386&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jcis.2019.12.132&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic layer deposition of Al2O3 on P2-Na0.5Mn0.5Co0.5O2 as interfacial layer for high power sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ramasamy, Hari Vignesh; Didwal, Pravin N.; Sinha, Soumyadeep; Aravindan, Vanchiappan; Heo, Jaeyeong; Park, Chan-Jin; Lee, Yun-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">564</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">467-477</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Surface modification is one of the impressive and widely used technique to improve the electrochem. performance of sodium-ion batteries by modifying the electrode-electrolyte interface.  Herein, we used the at. layer deposition (ALD) to modify the surface of P2-Na0.5Mn0.5Co0.5O2 by sub-monolayer Al2O3 coating on the prefabricated electrodes.  Phase purity is confirmed using various structural and morphol. studies.  The pristine electrode delivered an initial discharge capacity of 154 mAh g-1 at 0.5C, and inferior rate performance of 23 mAh g-1 at 40C rate.  On the other hand, the interfacial modified cathode with 5 cycles of ALD coating delivers a high capacity of 174 and 45 mAh g-1 at 0.5C and 40C rate, resp.  The Co2+/3+ redox couple is utilized for the faradaic process with high reversibility along with suppressed P2-O2 phase transition.  The presence of the Al2O3 layer acts as an artificial cathode electrolyte interface by suppressing the electrolyte oxidn. at higher cutoff potentials.  This is clearly validated by the reduced charge transfer resistance of surface modified electrodes after cycling at various current rates.
